# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/terraform--v1.10.3` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/terraform--v1.10.3$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Code Review: Terraform Plan/Apply Evaluation Pipeline

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/terraform--v1.10.3 (mirror of hashicorp/terraform)
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Category**: code-review
- **Task Type**: repo-clone

## Description

You are reviewing a recently merged pull request that modifies Terraform's plan/apply evaluation pipeline. The PR touches the expression evaluator, input variable processor, apply orchestrator, and hook dispatch system. The stated goal was to improve deferred resource handling and ephemeral variable support, but several defects were introduced during the merge — both functional bugs and cross-component interaction errors.

Your task is to **find the defects and produce a structured review report with proposed fixes**.

## Context

The changes span four core areas of Terraform's evaluation infrastructure:

1. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** — Expression evaluation engine: implements `GetInputVariable()`, `GetResource()`, and `GetModule()` on the `evaluationStateData` struct. These functions resolve references to variables, resources, and modules during graph walks. `GetInputVariable()` handles special behavior during the validate walk (returning unknown values) and marks values as sensitive/ephemeral. `GetResource()` handles unknown instance keys for deferred resources and decodes resource state.

2. **`internal/terraform/eval_variable.go`** — Input variable processing: `prepareFinalInputVariableValue()` converts raw input values through type checking, default substitution, nullable handling, and mark application (sensitive/ephemeral). Called during both plan and apply walks to prepare variables for evaluation.

3. **`internal/terraform/context_apply.go`** — Apply orchestration: `ApplyAndEval()` validates apply-time variables via `checkApplyTimeVariables()`, constructs the apply graph, and executes the graph walk. It also fires import hooks for resources with `Importing` set in the plan changes.

4. **`internal/terraform/hook.go`** — Hook dispatch interface: defines `HookAction` constants (`HookActionContinue`, `HookActionHalt`) and the `Hook` interface with `PreApply`/`PostApply` methods. `NilHook` provides default no-op implementations that return `HookActionContinue` — all custom hooks embed `NilHook` and override only what they need.

## Task

Review the files listed above for the following types of defects:

- **Functional bugs**: Logic errors that cause incorrect behavior (e.g., inverted conditions, wrong return values, missing state updates).
- **Cross-file interaction bugs**: Defects where a change in one file breaks assumptions in another file (e.g., hook dispatch returning Halt instead of Continue causes all apply operations to abort).
- **Data integrity bugs**: Missing marks, lost sensitivity flags, or incorrect type handling that leads to data leaks or panics.

For each defect you find:

1. **Describe the defect** in your review report.
2. **Write a fix** as a unified diff in the `fix_patch` field.

**Do NOT edit source files directly.** Express all fixes as unified diffs in your review report. The evaluation system will apply your patches and verify correctness.

### Expected Output

After completing your review, write a JSON file at `/workspace/review.json` containing an array of defect objects:

```json
[
  {
    "file": "internal/terraform/evaluate.go",
    "line": 281,
    "severity": "critical",
    "description": "Brief description of what is wrong and why",
    "fix_patch": "--- a/internal/terraform/evaluate.go\n+++ b/internal/terraform/evaluate.go\n@@ -278,5 +278,5 @@\n-    old line\n+    new line\n"
  }
]
```

Each entry must include:
- `file` — Relative path from repository root
- `line` — Approximate line number where the defect occurs
- `severity` — One of: `critical`, `high`, `medium`, `low`
- `description` — What the defect is and what impact it has
- `fix_patch` — Unified diff showing the proposed fix (use `--- a/` and `+++ b/` prefix format)

## Evaluation

Your review will be evaluated on:
- **Detection accuracy** (50%): Precision and recall of reported defects
- **Fix quality** (50%): Whether your proposed patches correctly resolve the defects

## Constraints

- **Time limit**: 1200 seconds
- Do NOT edit source files directly — express fixes only in `fix_patch`
- Do NOT run tests — the evaluation system handles verification

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user provided a hard code review task for a Terraform repository mirrored at `github.com/sg-evals/terraform--v1.10.3`. The goal is to find defects in 4 specific files that were modified by a PR focused on "deferred resource handling and ephemeral variable support." The user requires:
   - Detection of **functional bugs**, **cross-file interaction bugs**, and **data integrity bugs**
   - A `review.json` file written to `/workspace/review.json` containing an array of defect objects
   - Each defect must include: `file`, `line`, `severity`, `description`, and `fix_patch` (unified diff)
   - The evaluation system will apply patches and run tests to verify correctness
   - Tests must NOT be run manually

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Terraform Core evaluation pipeline**: `evaluationStateData`, `GetInputVariable()`, `GetResource()`, `GetModule()`
   - **cty marks**: Sensitive (`marks.Sensitive`) and Ephemeral (`marks.Ephemeral`) marks applied to cty values; marks are set-based (idempotent when applied twice)
   - **HookAction constants**: `HookActionContinue = 0` (iota), `HookActionHalt = 1`; NilHook embeds for no-op implementations
   - **Hook dispatch mechanism**: `ctx.Hook()` in `eval_context_builtin.go` iterates hooks, propagates errors, and handles `HookActionHalt` by returning nil (early exit)
   - **DeferralAllowed**: Flag in `graphWalkOpts` controlling whether resources can be deferred during a walk
   - **Named values**: `namedvals.State` stores input variable values as-is (preserves marks)
   - **prepareFinalInputVariableValue()**: Handles type coercion, defaults, n
... (truncated)

210-assistanttext-
Written `/workspace/review.json` with two confirmed defects:

**Bug 1 (critical) — `context_apply.go:153`: Hook return values silently discarded**

The `for _, h := range c.hooks` loop calls `h.PreApplyImport()` and `h.PostApplyImport()` but throws away the `(HookAction, error)` return values. Both the `stopHook` (used for graceful shutdown) and any user-implemented hooks that return errors or `HookActionHalt` are completely ignored. The fix checks `err` and `action` after each hook call and returns early when either condition signals a halt/error.

**Bug 2 (high) — `context_apply.go:191`: `DeferralAllowed: true` hardcoded during apply**

The plan walk (`context_plan.go:723`) correctly passes `DeferralAllowed: opts.DeferralAllowed`, which is `false` for standard Terraform (only the stacks runtime sets it to `true`). The apply walk hardcodes `true`, which:
- Makes `Deferrals.DeferralAllowed()` return `true`, causing `node_module_expand.go` to allow unknown `for_each`/`count` values during apply
- Allows resources encountering unexpected unknown values during apply to silently defer themselves rather than error

The stacks runtime has its own apply path and does not use `context_apply.go`, so the correct value is `false`.

Technically we should always return\n376: \t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n377: \t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n378: \t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n379: \t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n380: \t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n381: \t// validation.\n382: \t//\n383: \t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n384: \t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n385: \t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n386: \t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n387: \tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n388: \t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n389: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n390: \t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n391: \t\t}\n392: \t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n393: \n394: \t\tswitch {\n395: \t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n396: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n397: \t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n398: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n399: \t\tdefault:\n400: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n401: \t\t}\n402: \t}\n403: \n404: \t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n405: \t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n406: \t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n407: \t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n408: \tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n409: \tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n410: \tif !known {\n411: \t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n412: \t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n413: \t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n414: \t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n415: \t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n416: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n417: \t}\n418: \n419: \tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n420: \t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n421: \t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n422: \t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n423: \n424: \t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n425: \t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n426: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n427: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n428: \t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n429: \n430: \t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n431: \t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n432: \t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n433: \t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n434: \t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n435: \t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n436: \t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n437: \t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n438: \t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n439: \t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n440: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n441: \t\t\t}\n442: \t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n443: \t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n447: \t}\n448: \n449: \tswitch instKeyType {\n450: \n451: \tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n452: \t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n453: \t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n454: \t\t// implementation.\n455: \t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n456: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n459: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n460: \t\treturn ret, diags\n461: \n462: \tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n463: \t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n464: \t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n465: \t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n466: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n467: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n468: \t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n469: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n470: \t\t}\n471: \t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n472: \n473: \tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n474: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n475: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n476: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n477: \t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n478: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n479: \t\t}\n480: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n481: \n482: \tdefault:\n483: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n484: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n485: \t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n486: \t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n487: \t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n488: \t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n489: \t\t\t),\n490: \t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n491: \t\t})\n492: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n493: \t}\n494: }\n495: \n496: func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n497: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n498: \t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n499: \t// name is declared at all.\n500: \tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n501: \tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(moduleAddr)\n502: \tif moduleConfig == nil {\n503: \t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n504: \t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n505: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n506: \t}\n507: \n508: \tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n509: \t}\n518: \n519: \t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n520: \t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n521: \t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n522: \t//\n523: \t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n524: \t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n528: \t// runtime.\n529: \t//\n530: \t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n531: \t// would be nice to can't even predict what the result type will be because it\n539: \t\t\t// would be either an object or tuple type decided based on the instance\n540: \t\t\t// keys.\n541: \t\t\t// (We can't get in below.)\n544: \t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n545: \n546: \t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n547: \t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n548: \t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n549: \t\t\t}\n550: \t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n551: \t\t}\n552: \t}\n553: \n554: \t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n555: \t// state available in all cases.\n556: \t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n557: \t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n558: \tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n561: \t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n562: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n563: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n564: \t\t\tSummary: This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n566: \t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n567: \t\t})\n568: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n569: \t}\n570: \tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n571: \n572: \tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n573: \t\t// FIXME: This does not yet work with deferrals, and it would be nice to\n574: \t\t// find some way to refactor this so that the following code is not so\n575: \t\t// tethered to the current implementation details. Instead we should\n576: \t\t// have an abstract idea of first determining what instances the\n577: \t\t// resource has (using d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys) and\n578: \t\t// then retrieving the value for each instance to assemble into the\n579: \t\t// result, using some per-resource-mode logic maintained elsewhere.\n580: \t\treturn d.getEphemeralResource(addr, rng)\n581: \t}\n582: \n583: \trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n584: \n585: \tif rs == nil {\n586: \t\tswitch d.Operation {\n587: \t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n588: \t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n589: \t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n590: \t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n591: \t\t\tswitch {\n592: \t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n593: \t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n594: \t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n595: \t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n596: \t\t\tdefault:\n597: \t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n598: \t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n599: \t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n600: \t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n601: \t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n602: \t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n603: \t\t\t\t// continue.\n604: \t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n605: \t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n606: \t\t\t}\n607: \n608: \t\tcase walkImport:\n609: \t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n610: \t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n611: \t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n612: \t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n613: \t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n614: \t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n615: \t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n616: \t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n617: \t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n618: \t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n645: \t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n646: \tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n647: \t\tinstances[key] = value\n648: \t}\n649: \n650: \t// Decode all instances in the current state\n651: \tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n652: \tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n653: \t\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\n654: \t\t\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\n655: \t\t\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\n656: \t\t\tcontinue\n657: \t\t}\n658: \t\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\n659: \n660: \t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n661: \t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n662: \t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n663: \t\t\tcontinue\n664: \t\t}\n665: \n666: \t\t\t\t}\n677: \t\t\t}\n678: \t\t}\n679: \n680: \t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n681: \t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n682: \t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n683: \t\t\tif change == nil {\n684: \t\t\t\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\n685: \t\t\t\t// lookup an individual \t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n702: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n703: \t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n704: \t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n705: \t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n706: \t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n707: \t\t\t})\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \n711: \t\tval := ios.Value\n712: \n713: \t\tinstances[key] = val\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n717: \tvar \t}\n786: \n787: \treturn ret, diags\n788: }\n789: \n790: func (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n791: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n792: \n793: \tif d.Operation == walkValidate || d.Operation == walkEval {\n794: \t\t// Ephemeral instances are never live during the validate walk. Eval is\n795: \t\t// similarly offline, and since there is no value stored we can't return\n796: \t\t// anything other than dynamic.\n797: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n798: \t}\n799: \n800: \t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n801: \t// or resources that are in the state.\n802: \tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n803: \n804: \t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n805: \t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n806: \t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n807: \tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n808: \t\tinstances[key] = value\n809: \t}\n810: \n811: \tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n812: \tkeyType, keys, haveUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(absAddr)\n813: \tif haveUnknownKeys {\n814: \t\t// We can probably do better than totally unknown at least for a\n815: \t\t// single-instance resource, but we'll just keep it simple for now.\n816: \t\t// Result must be marked as ephemeral so that we can still catch\n817: \t\t// attempts to use the results in non-ephemeral locations, so that\n818: \t\t// the operator doesn't end up trapped with an error on a subsequent\n819: \t\t// plan/apply round.\n820: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n821: \t}\n822: \n823: \tephems := d.Evaluator.EphemeralResources\n824: \tgetInstValue := func(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n825: \t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n826: \n827: \t\t// If we have a deferred instance with this key we don't need to check if it is live or not,\n828: \t\t// it has not been created so we can just return the deferred value.\n829: \t\tif v, ok := instances[addr.Resource.Key]; ok {\n830: \t\t\treturn v, diags\n831: \t\t}\n832: \n833: \t\tval, isLive := ephems.InstanceValue(addr)\n834: \t\tif !isLive {\n835: \t\t\t// If the instance is no longer \"live\" by the time we're accessing\n836: \t\t\t// it then that suggests that it needed renewal and renewal has\n837: \t\t\t// failed, and so the object's value is no longer usable. We'll\n838: \t\t\t// still return the value in case it's somehow useful for diagnosis,\n839: \t\t\t// but we return an error to prevent further evaluation of whatever\n840: \t\t\t// other expression In that case, Apply will use a default set of options.
